  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/391633264?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elevetha " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elevetha " href="/user/show/11828657-elevetha">Elevetha </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Lovers of fairytales retold, reimagined, or twisted on it's side</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11828657-elevetha?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11828657-elevetha?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11828657-elevetha?shelf=gorgeous-covers">gorgeous-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11828657-elevetha?shelf=fairytale-retelling">fairytale-retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11828657-elevetha?shelf=quite-good">quite-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11828657-elevetha?shelf=fairytales">fairytales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11828657-elevetha?shelf=magic-and-other-magical-substances">magic-and-other-magical-substances</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer391633264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15848269907809762619">Excited!!<br/><br/>IT'S HERE!! <br/><br/>Now that's what I call quality shipping....<br/><br/>It's so pretty. And, holla! It's longer than the other two.<br/><br/>*Edit*<br/><br/>3.5 stars.<br/><br/>I liked it a lot. Not as much as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3697927.Princess_of_the_Midnight_Ball__Princess__1_' title='Princess of the Midnight Ball (Princess #1) by Jessica Day George' rel='nofollow noopener'>Princess of the Midnight Ball</a> but more so than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7199667.Princess_of_Glass__Princess__2_' title='Princess of Glass (Princess #2) by Jessica Day George' rel='nofollow noopener'>Princess of Glass</a>.<br/><br/>Red Riding Hood, Robin Hood, AND The Twelve Dancing Princesses?! EEP.<br/><br/><br/>Cover: They match! They match!! *does dance of joy* They are so pretty....<br/><br/>Story: I was slightly confused at times. It was choppy and there were too many things being thrown at you at once. <br/><br/>Chara</span>
  <span id="freeText15848269907809762619" style="display:none">Excited!!<br /><br />IT'S HERE!! <br /><br />Now that's what I call quality shipping....<br /><br />It's so pretty. And, holla! It's longer than the other two.<br /><br />*Edit*<br /><br />3.5 stars.<br /><br />I liked it a lot. Not as much as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3697927.Princess_of_the_Midnight_Ball__Princess__1_" title="Princess of the Midnight Ball (Princess #1) by Jessica Day George" rel="nofollow noopener">Princess of the Midnight Ball</a> but more so than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7199667.Princess_of_Glass__Princess__2_" title="Princess of Glass (Princess #2) by Jessica Day George" rel="nofollow noopener">Princess of Glass</a>.<br /><br />Red Riding Hood, Robin Hood, AND The Twelve Dancing Princesses?! EEP.<br /><br /><br />Cover: They match! They match!! *does dance of joy* They are so pretty....<br /><br />Story: I was slightly confused at times. It was choppy and there were too many things being thrown at you at once. <br /><br />Characters: <br /><br />Petunia: I must say I rather loved her. She was smart. Brave. Not nearly as sassy as Poppy. *boo* She carries a pistol and matches with her wherever she goes. Good friends with awesome brothers-in-law, Galen and Heinrich. (I'm sorry, who wouldn't love those two?) She is willing to sacrifice a lot for family and those she cares about.<br /><br />I really found one aspect of her character fascinating. The fact that she was so little when she was cursed. That was all she'd ever known. Dancing and dancing every night. Her sisters being slowly torn apart by the curse. But Pet was so small. That was her life. When the curse was broken, she didn't shun dancing. She didn't quite understand what had happened nor what was going on. So she ended up, I felt, quite different from her sisters.<br /><br /><br />Oliver: You didn't quite live up to Galen standards but close. Close.<br /><br />Oliver is an earl. Or was. Before the war and the witchcraft accusations being thrown around and his earldom getting ripped away and handed off to others. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Gregori and the "Grandmother". I think that's how it goes.... It was rather confusing. But that could have been just the effects of the unholy hours of the morning. *slaps myself* Bad Elevetha. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />He is a Wolf of the Wolves of Westfalin Woods. (bwah hah hah) And, while robbing (ROBIN HOOD, BABY!!) Petunia's carriage, he has a pistol aimed at his head. What a way to meet your future love interest. She's petite and has a pistol she isn't afraid to use. He should be scared. Well, shenanigans ensue and he ends up abducting her. And taking her home to meet Mother.<br /><br /><br />Mother: Oliver, darling. You poor sweet thing. Be a good boy and escort her to where she was going originally.<br /><br />Oliver: *confused*<br /><br />Petunia: *equally confused*<br /><br />Mother: I knew your mother, dear.<br /><br />Petunia and Oliver: Oooh. Gotcha now.<br /><br />....<br /><br />The King Under Stone is back. Well, one of his sons has ascended the throne and is out to fetch him and his brothers some brides.<br /><br />And Petunia, being a sweet dear willing to do most anything for family and wishing to be rid of this curse hanging over their family once and for all, ventures into the Kingdom Under Stone....<br /><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ This one ties back an awful lot to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3697927.Princess_of_the_Midnight_Ball__Princess__1_" title="Princess of the Midnight Ball (Princess #1) by Jessica Day George" rel="nofollow noopener">Princess of the Midnight Ball</a>. Quite a lot of the same ideas floating around but, even though it was slightly repetitive, I didn't mind so much.<br /><br /><br />Also, the fact that none of the girls could have children because of the curse placed on their mother by King Under Stone was heartbreaking. I felt so sad for Rose and Lily esp.<br /><br />And poor Jonquil! She did not fare well in the years between the first book and this one. Broken inside, the poor dear. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I LOVED that ending! Not as much as for what we got on Oliver and Petunia, but what we got on some of the others characters. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Lily and Rose are EXPECTING!!!!! There was much squeeing on my part when that was revealed.<br /><br />And Galen and Rose are knitting baby blankets and cocoons! So adorable. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />A wholly enjoyable, wonderfully satisfying book and ending to a great fairytale series.<br /><br />Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15848269907809762619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_476428578" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/476428578" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/999233-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594609442p2/999233.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/476428578?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/999233-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/999233-laura?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/999233-laura?shelf=review-on-blog">review-on-blog</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/999233-laura?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/999233-laura?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/999233-laura?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer476428578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17473669198762937884">This story certainly started off well! I was captivated and wanted to know more about the spunky heroine and her adventures. The cover was eye-catching (without being cliche) and I loved the fantastic flowing red cape. There was one aspect that made me grimace: love at first sight. Ugh.<br/><br/>Usually the whole oh-I-fell-in-love-at-first-sight thing kinda bothers me. (What am I doing using that flimsy word "kinda" when I really mean, "totally infuriates"?) And initially I was annoyed because this novel </span>
  <span id="freeText17473669198762937884" style="display:none">This story certainly started off well! I was captivated and wanted to know more about the spunky heroine and her adventures. The cover was eye-catching (without being cliche) and I loved the fantastic flowing red cape. There was one aspect that made me grimace: love at first sight. Ugh.<br /><br />Usually the whole oh-I-fell-in-love-at-first-sight thing kinda bothers me. (What am I doing using that flimsy word "kinda" when I really mean, "totally infuriates"?) And initially I was annoyed because this novel was starting to follow the same typical pattern. But then my view kind of shifted. Strangely enough, it was the author's use of magic that convinced me this scenario was different. Even the characters in the story addressed the whole love at first sight predicament. They acknowledged the craziness of it and even seemed to poke a little fun while doing so. And for some reason, that made my usual feelings of unrest totally at ease. I was completely fine with the whole love at first sight syndrome because it was illustrated in this magical realm where strange things happen. And hey, if girls can magically be trapped in a creepy underworld at night and forced to dance until their slippers wore out, why can't they magically fall in love at first sight too?<br /><br />Okay, mini rant over. Here are some other things I noticed about the book. It was pretty clean, so no objectionable content. The characters were interesting; they weren't flat or superficial. There were definitely parts in the story where I was particularly muddled because I didn't know HOW the characters were going to get out of their unfortunate situations. I enjoyed seeing the sisters together again and was dismayed at the idea of them all having to go back to the King Under Stone. I also was pretty involved in the story and I think I read it in one sitting. I didn't like the ending though. Maybe because it seemed rushed (especially at the climax,) but I wanted a longer explanation, a prolonged dramatic conclusion. Everything seemed to resolve in a short span of pages and that was a little disappointing. The ending also seemed a little too reminiscent of the first book. But all in all, Princess of the Silver Woods was entertaining, fun main characters, and an interesting story line. Fans of Shannon Hale should also check out this series. I'd recommend.<br /><br />*Thanks to Bloomsbury for allowing me to be part of the blog tour and providing a copy through Netgalley in exchange for my honest review.<br /><br />**Taken from My Sentiments Exactly!: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://reviewsatmse.blogspot.com/2013/01/princess-of-silver-woods-blog-tour.html">http://reviewsatmse.blogspot.com/2013...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17473669198762937884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_224569662" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/224569662" />
    <a title="Valerie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1879727-valerie"><img alt="Valerie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257225221p2/1879727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/224569662?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valerie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valerie" href="/user/show/1879727-valerie">Valerie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1879727-valerie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1879727-valerie?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer224569662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13801869976942549218">This seems to happen quite a bit when I read one of Jessica Day George's books. At first I get all excited and can't wait for the book to come out. Then I get the book and start reading it as soon as possible. The beginning is great and I start believing this is going to be her best book yet. Then somewhere near the end it gets a little weird. I think it may have to do with the magic of the world. Sometimes it doesn't make sense, like it wasn't fully fleshed out or something. <br/><br/>This is the third b</span>
  <span id="freeText13801869976942549218" style="display:none">This seems to happen quite a bit when I read one of Jessica Day George's books. At first I get all excited and can't wait for the book to come out. Then I get the book and start reading it as soon as possible. The beginning is great and I start believing this is going to be her best book yet. Then somewhere near the end it gets a little weird. I think it may have to do with the magic of the world. Sometimes it doesn't make sense, like it wasn't fully fleshed out or something. <br /><br />This is the third book in the twelve dancing princess series featuring Petunia (the youngest). She goes to Westfalin but on her way there she encounters bandits-one of them being Oliver. This however, is not her only problem. The new King Under Stone and his brothers are still out to get the sisters. <br /><br />I'm glad I got to see more of the sisters, though it is mostly Petunia and Oliver in the beginning. Oliver kind of reminds me of Robin Hood so that was cool. Almost like a retelling for both main characters.<br /><br />I like all the princesses that have been featured in this series by George for different reasons. Petunia is spunky (I suppose that is what you call a short girl that has a backbone), though she has her vulnerability. Petunia and Oliver are a charming duo. I'd say cute but usually leave that reserved for puppies and babies.<br /><br />I'm not a huge fan of love at first sight in books, most of the time it seems the guy/girl just seems to think the person is beautiful/handsome and that is mostly what they base there love on from there. In most cases I'm okay with it and this one handled it well enough, it's not <i>exactly</i> love at first sight. <br /><br />Too bad this is the last of the series, but it ended well. I recommend the series to fairy tales lovers. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13801869976942549218" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_261041777" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/261041777" />
    <a title="Erin " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2997696-erin"><img alt="Erin " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531863934p2/2997696.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/261041777?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin " href="/user/show/2997696-erin">Erin </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer261041777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15451717059798237842">I am a little sad that this is the final installment of the Twelve Dancing Princesses series, but that aside I must applaud Jessica Day George for putting forth a wonderful conclusion to her trilogy. Princess of the Silver Woods is a delightful read and a shining example of George's ability to reinvent the well known into something enchantingly original. <br/><br/>Before I get into Oliver and Petunia's tale I want to say how impressed I was with George's treatment of Galen and Rose. The first book in a se</span>
  <span id="freeText15451717059798237842" style="display:none">I am a little sad that this is the final installment of the Twelve Dancing Princesses series, but that aside I must applaud Jessica Day George for putting forth a wonderful conclusion to her trilogy. Princess of the Silver Woods is a delightful read and a shining example of George's ability to reinvent the well known into something enchantingly original. <br /><br />Before I get into Oliver and Petunia's tale I want to say how impressed I was with George's treatment of Galen and Rose. The first book in a series always holds a special place with readers, but unfortunately the main characters of those books tend to fall by the wayside as they become supporting cast members of later installments. Princess of the Silver Woods is a rare exception in that the title couple have their moments, but they do not eclipse the strengths exhibited by the original couple in the first story. I really appreciate George for the obvious care she took in crafting this piece and her dedication both to her readers and the continuity of her work.<br /><br />The Princess of the Silver Woods is told from Petunia's point of view. The youngest of the twelve sisters she was but six years old when George first took her readers to Westfalin. Now sixteen, Petunia wants nothing more than to be seen as the independent young woman she is. George showcases Petunia's personality and character by integrating it with that of Little Red Riding Hood. I really liked the idea and while I feel it worked in the author's favor, this strength also made the less impressive link between Oliver and Robin Hood all the more evident. It starts out strong, but doesn't maintain momentum through the entire novel, something I found very frustrating as George managed it so nicely with her heroine.<br /><br />Maybe not as impressive as the opening volume of the series, but a worthwhile conclusion nonetheless. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15451717059798237842" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer275034490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2438145522255507010">The third book in <i>The Princesses of Westfalin Trilogy</i> by Jessica Day George. Princess Petunia is on her way to visit the Grand Duchess Volenskaya when her coach is detained by bandits in wolf masks. A series of mishaps has the princess and her coach escaping only to have an accident down the road. There she ends up being kidnapped by the bandits and taken to their home. Oliver is really an Earl but after the war, his lands were divided and given away. He and his family live in a forgotten estate</span>
  <span id="freeText2438145522255507010" style="display:none">The third book in <i>The Princesses of Westfalin Trilogy</i> by Jessica Day George. Princess Petunia is on her way to visit the Grand Duchess Volenskaya when her coach is detained by bandits in wolf masks. A series of mishaps has the princess and her coach escaping only to have an accident down the road. There she ends up being kidnapped by the bandits and taken to their home. Oliver is really an Earl but after the war, his lands were divided and given away. He and his family live in a forgotten estate and he is forced to rob from the rich to give to his poor.<br /><br />It's been a while since I read the first 2 books but it wasn't hard to follow. As stated in the description, the stories of Robin Hood and Red Riding Hood are touched on in the book. The hero, Oliver, being both Robin Hood and the wolf, at first. Petunia wears a red hooded cloak, hence the "red riding hood". Then there is the issue of the "12 dancing princesses" and the King Under Stone that comes back to haunt them. <br /><br />I felt it was a good addition to the series but it wasn't my favorite. Though I did love Petunia and I did like Oliver, I would have liked more page time with the two together. Plus, this book takes place quite a while after the other two. Which, since it involves the youngest princess, I guess it had to. But I did like it and enjoyed reading it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2438145522255507010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText1760287698280721316" style="display:none">The third of the 12 Dancing Princesses stories is a retelling of Little Red Riding Hood and it s just as delightful as the first two books. Petunia is the youngest sister and as such has slightly different memories of the King under stone and all that happened to her as a small child. When her carriage is stopped by highwaymen dressed as wolves she doesn't hesitate to fight back. Quite well. Which gifts her with an unusual friendship with a young man. When she discovers that someone she is supposed to trust has actually betrayed her and her sisters she discovers that new alliances can be extremely helpful. It's a delightful story with another of George's signature vibrant heroines.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1797277807870564771">A satisfying conclusion to a thrilling fairy tale trilogy. <br/><br/><br/><br/>This book exceeded my expectations as the third and final book in this fantastic fairy tale series. It picks up the threads of the original tale and knits them into a brand new follow up, blending new characters, and familiar favorites, in this Red Ring Hood and Twelve Dancing Princesses mash-up that hits all the right notes. <br/><br/><br/><br/>Petunia is a brave young woman, who has already faced unimaginable danger from the time she was barely able to wa</span>
  <span id="freeText1797277807870564771" style="display:none">A satisfying conclusion to a thrilling fairy tale trilogy. <br /><br /><br /><br />This book exceeded my expectations as the third and final book in this fantastic fairy tale series. It picks up the threads of the original tale and knits them into a brand new follow up, blending new characters, and familiar favorites, in this Red Ring Hood and Twelve Dancing Princesses mash-up that hits all the right notes. <br /><br /><br /><br />Petunia is a brave young woman, who has already faced unimaginable danger from the time she was barely able to walk. I liked how she took initiative, and is constantly thinking ahead, though she does have her weaknesses as well. <br /><br /><br /><br />Oliver and his family is a wonderful addition to this world, he is a courageous leader, and I love his strong sense of loyalty. <br /><br /><br /><br />I loved how this book brought back all of the sisters and their husbands, especially Galen and Rose, as well bringing back the dangers from the very first book in a fresh, credible new way, adding more to the depth of the Westfalian lore and history. All in all it was a very quick, but satisfying read. And I loved how it kind of came full circle in a way, to the first story that started it all. Plus, as a fellow knitter and crocheter, I couldn't help but love the bone thrown to needle-crafters! Definitely recommend!<br /><br /><br /><br />I received a complimentary ecopy of this book. Opinions expressed in this review are completely my own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1797277807870564771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_428298824" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/428298824" />
    <a title="Kara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6137018-kara"><img alt="Kara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482283420p2/6137018.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/428298824?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kara" href="/user/show/6137018-kara">Kara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer428298824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6906719039858975419">Here it is!!<br/><br/>Minor Spoilers<br/><br/>My Review<br/>Wow, what a great story! I highly recommend you read Princess of the Midnight Ball before reading this princess story because it’s the same family from a different perspective. Petunia is the youngest of 12 princesses and this book is her journey. She is on the way to visit the Grand Duchess Volenskaya when her royal coach is threatened and almost robbed. That’s when her adventure starts and she gradually learns that villains are not always evil looking and tru</span>
  <span id="freeText6906719039858975419" style="display:none">Here it is!!<br /><br />Minor Spoilers<br /><br />My Review<br />Wow, what a great story! I highly recommend you read Princess of the Midnight Ball before reading this princess story because it’s the same family from a different perspective. Petunia is the youngest of 12 princesses and this book is her journey. She is on the way to visit the Grand Duchess Volenskaya when her royal coach is threatened and almost robbed. That’s when her adventure starts and she gradually learns that villains are not always evil looking and true heroes are not always dressed in fine clothing.<br /><br />Oliver is impressed with Petunia from the moment they meet and he is determined to keep her safe. Then he comes across the shadow men lurking outside Petunia’s window and makes a decision to protect her even if it places his own life in danger. Oliver has learned to be a leader since he was a teenager, but due to several injustices his family has suffered greatly. He’s finally ready to set things right, but what will it cost to have justice prevail?<br /><br />These 12 princesses have such different personalities and Petunia became my favorite of the sisters in this book! The princesses are: daisy, hyacinth, iris, jonquil, lilac, lily, orchid, pansy, petunia, poppy, rose, and violet. For years Petunia and her sisters were forced to obey the King Under Stone, dancing each night with the 12 princes. It brought despair, broken dancing shoes, and trauma to the princesses and to their household. Now they are free of this evil, but there’s a new King Under Stone and he wants to finish what his father started. Petunia is 16 now and she is ready for battle. Not only can she fire a gun fearlessly, but she is bold and incredibly feisty. Her nightmares are back and worse than ever, but this time with the help of her sisters and their husbands Petunia is ready to defend herself. The only thing I didn’t enjoy about this story was that their father, the king, is only in the story towards the middle and at the end. He is jaded by what has taken place in his own kingdom and has no place in protecting his daughters. However, every character from Midnight Ball is in this story and it’s a satisfying ending. <br /> <br />I knew I would love this story from the beginning and within the first 50 pages I couldn’t put it down. There is true love, betrayal, evil, good bandits, and 12 incredible princesses that endure both good and bad together. I highly recommend Princess of the Silver Woods for both fans of Jessica Day George as well those who will be reading her book for the first time. She understands how to write an incredible adventure with several characters without confusing the story or slowing the action down! Even though this book is from Petunia’s (and also Oliver’s) perspective, the reader is experiencing the heart of each princess as the story unfolds. There is violence (gun shots, one gunshot wound, a few deaths, one botched robbery, and vivid nightmares) and a few uses of the word bast*rd, but otherwise very appropriate and quite enjoyable. It was also a thrill seeing the references to Red Riding Hood and Robin Hood in this exciting tale that is both pleasing and endearing to any reader who enjoys fantasy books. This is easily my favorite Jessica Day George book and I look forward to reading more of her books. <br /><br /><br /> I want to thank Bloomsbury USA Children’s Books and Netgalley for the free ebook ARC they provided for review purposes. I was not required to write a positive review. The opinions expressed are my own. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6906719039858975419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer5913409629573150061">I love the twelve dancing princesses story! It is one of my very favorite fairy tales! I have read many different versions, yet I keep coming back to Jessica Day George's retelling. She begins with her first in the series, Princess of the Midnight Ball, followed by the second in the series, Princess of Glass. Each story gives a unique perspective to the magic and curse surrounding the twelve princesses. The third and final book in the series, Princess of the Silver Woods, did not disappoint! It </span>
  <span id="freeText5913409629573150061" style="display:none">I love the twelve dancing princesses story! It is one of my very favorite fairy tales! I have read many different versions, yet I keep coming back to Jessica Day George's retelling. She begins with her first in the series, Princess of the Midnight Ball, followed by the second in the series, Princess of Glass. Each story gives a unique perspective to the magic and curse surrounding the twelve princesses. The third and final book in the series, Princess of the Silver Woods, did not disappoint! It incorporated even more fairy tales into the story, like Robin Hood and Little Red Riding Hood. The book was fast-paced and all of my favorite characters were there! Some new characters were introduced, some likeable and some that were not. I felt myself trying to figure out who was really good and who was putting on a facade! In this final installment of the Princess series, Princess of the Silver Woods will have you on your toes as you take the adventure of a life-time! Bravo, five stars to Jessica Day George! I love her work and can't wait to see what she has in store for us next!<br />I received a copy of this book for free via Netgalley. This is my honest review.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13262697216678927170">This was a great book with lots of interesting characters and a great plot that pulls you in. This was a fairy tale retelling based on a combination of "The Twelve Dancing Princesses", "Little Red Riding Hood", & "Robin Hood". The main influence came from "The Twelve Dancing Princesses" with details from "Little Red Riding Hood", & "Robin Hood" thrown in along with the authors own original additions to make a very entertaining story. This was the third book in it's series however it is not neces</span>
  <span id="freeText13262697216678927170" style="display:none">This was a great book with lots of interesting characters and a great plot that pulls you in. This was a fairy tale retelling based on a combination of "The Twelve Dancing Princesses", "Little Red Riding Hood", &amp; "Robin Hood". The main influence came from "The Twelve Dancing Princesses" with details from "Little Red Riding Hood", &amp; "Robin Hood" thrown in along with the authors own original additions to make a very entertaining story. This was the third book in it's series however it is not necessary to have read the previous two to understand and enjoy this one although I am sure they would add to it. I loved reading about how Petunia and Oliver met and watching how their relationship grew throughout this book and also enjoyed seeing how Petunia and her sisters interacted with one another. I am definitely planning on reading the first two books in this series as well as other books by this author.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vAwrbHBP2Fv5zoUi0LVWrV5Sr0lJJPABiL5MMWGt7X+ytlXRgZ3rZJTVU4xRD4BOgdi1MpF2kvgyrl+/9J31ew==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iqzQcNd1KRukUR152nqHmF8P5//en8vNiBLvGoaJJHWEFq7NJqcaJMlKy9dbwFF7gIX9hAbNqTQyAvyUE7k8cQ==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer14776912008535705883">Jessica Day George likes chocolate, knitting, books, travel, movies, dragons, horses, dogs, and her family. These are all things to keep in mind if you ever meet her. For instance, you could bring her chocolate to make the meeting go more smoothly. You could also talk about how adorable her children are, even if you have never seen them. You could discuss dog breeds (she had a Maltese named Pippin</span>
  <span id="freeText14776912008535705883" style="display:none">Jessica Day George likes chocolate, knitting, books, travel, movies, dragons, horses, dogs, and her family. These are all things to keep in mind if you ever meet her. For instance, you could bring her chocolate to make the meeting go more smoothly. You could also talk about how adorable her children are, even if you have never seen them. You could discuss dog breeds (she had a Maltese named Pippin, and grew up with a poodle mix and a Brittany Spaniel. Right now she has a Coton de Tulear named Sunny). You could talk about Norway, and how it's the Greatest Place On Earth, and Germany, The Second Greatest Place On Earth. You could ask her about yarn, and indicate a willingness to learn to knit your own socks, if you can't already do so.<br /><br />And, well, you could talk about books. Jessica's books, other people's books. It's really all about the books. To paraphrase Jerry Seinfeld: Friends, family, school, they were just obstacles in the way of getting more books.<br /><br />She would like it if books came with chocolate to eat while reading them.</span>

Together Galen and Rose will search for a way to break the curse that forces the princesses to dance at the midnight balls. All they need is one invisibility cloak, a black wool chain knit with enchanted silver needles, and that most critical ingredient of all—true love—to conquer their foes in the dark halls below. But malevolent forces are working against them above ground as well, and as cruel as the King Under Stone has seemed, his wrath is mere irritation compared to the evil that awaits Galen and Rose in
